Why is he on probation?’ Te evaṃ vadenti— They tell him everything, ‘ayaṃ, āvuso, bhikkhu dve saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajji dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo; eko māso saramānappaṭicchanno, eko māso assaramānappaṭicchanno. So saṃghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ dvemāsaparivāsaṃ yāci. Tassa saṃgho dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ dvemāsaparivāsaṃ adāsi. Tāyo ayaṃ, āvuso, bhikkhu āpanno tāsāyaṃ bhikkhu parivasatī’ti. So evaṃ vadeti— and he says, ‘yvāyaṃ, āvuso, māso saramānappaṭicchanno dhammikaṃ tassa māsassa parivāsadānaṃ; ‘The giving of probation for the month concealed while remembering it is legitimate, dhammattā ruhati. legal, and has effect. Yo ca khvāyaṃ, āvuso, māso assaramānappaṭicchanno adhammikaṃ tassa māsassa parivāsadānaṃ; The giving of probation for the month concealed without remembering it is illegitimate, adhammattā na ruhati. illegal, and has no effect. Ekassa, āvuso, māsassa bhikkhu mānattāraho’ti. He deserves the trial period only in relation to the one month.’

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu dve saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo; It may be that a monk has committed two offenses entailing suspension, both concealed for two months. eko māso nibbematikappaṭicchanno, eko māso vematikappaṭicchanno. He concealed one month while having no doubts about it, but the other while having doubts about it. So saṃghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ dvemāsaparivāsaṃ yācati. He asks the Order for probation for two months for both offenses, Tassa saṃgho dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ dvemāsaparivāsaṃ deti. and the Order gives him that probation. Tassa parivasantassa añño bhikkhu āgacchati bahussuto āgatāgamo dhammadharo vinayadharo mātikādharo paṇḍito viyatto medhāvī lajjī kukkuccako sikkhākāmo. While he is on probation, another monk arrives. He is learned, a master of the tradition; he is an expert on the Teaching, the Monastic Law, and the summaries; he is wise and competent, has sense of conscience, and is afraid of wrongdoing and fond of the training. So evaṃ vadeti— He says, ‘kiṃ ayaṃ, āvuso, bhikkhu āpanno? ‘What has this monk committed? Kissāyaṃ bhikkhu parivasatī’ti? Why is he on probation?’ Te evaṃ vadenti— They tell him everything, ‘ayaṃ, āvuso, bhikkhu dve saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajji dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo; eko māso nibbematikappaṭicchanno, eko māso vematikappaṭicchanno. So saṃghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ dvemāsaparivāsaṃ yāci. Tassa saṃgho dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ dvemāsaparivāsaṃ adāsi. Tāyo ayaṃ, āvuso, bhikkhu āpanno tāsāyaṃ bhikkhu parivasatī’ti. Yo ca khvāyaṃ, āvuso, māso vematikappaṭicchanno adhammikaṃ tassa māsassa parivāsadānaṃ; The giving of probation for the month concealed while having doubts about it is illegitimate, adhammattā na ruhati. illegal, and has no effect. Ekassa, āvuso, māsassa bhikkhu mānattāraho’”ti. He deserves the trial period only in relation to the one month.’”

2.5. Suddhantaparivāsa Purifying probation

Tena kho pana samayena aññataro bhikkhu sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpanno hoti. At one time a monk had committed many offenses entailing suspension. So āpattipariyantaṃ na jānāti; He did not know the number of offenses rattipariyantaṃ na jānāti; or the number of days/ āpattipariyantaṃ nassarati, rattipariyantaṃ nassarati; he did not remember the number of offenses or the number of days/ āpattipariyante vematiko, rattipariyante vematiko. he had doubts about the number of offenses and the number of days. So bhikkhūnaṃ ārocesi— He told the monks about this, “ahaṃ, āvuso, sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ; āpattipariyantaṃ na jānāmi, rattipariyantaṃ na jānāmi; āpattipariyantaṃ nassarāmi, rattipariyantaṃ nassarāmi; āpattipariyante vematiko, rattipariyante vematiko. Kathaṃ nu kho mayā paṭipajjitabban”ti? adding, “What should I do now?” Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. They told the Master and he said:

“Tena hi, bhikkhave, saṃgho tassa bhikkhuno tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ suddhantaparivāsaṃ detu. “Well then, the Order should give that monk a purifying probation for those offenses. Evañca pana, bhikkhave, dātabbo— And it should be given in this way:

Tena, bhikkhave, bhikkhunā saṃghaṃ upasaṅkamitvā … pe … That monk should approach the Order, put his upper robe over one shoulder, pay respect at the feet of the senior monks, squat on his heels, put the palms of his hands together, evamassa vacanīyo— and say:

‘ahaṃ, bhante, sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ. ‘Venerables, I have committed many offenses entailing suspension. Āpattipariyantaṃ na jānāmi, rattipariyantaṃ na jānāmi; I do not know the number of offenses or the number of days/ āpattipariyantaṃ nassarāmi, rattipariyantaṃ nassarāmi; I do not remember the number of offenses or the number of days/ āpattipariyante vematiko, rattipariyante vematiko. I have doubts about the number of offenses and the number of days. Sohaṃ, bhante, saṃghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ suddhantaparivāsaṃ yācāmī’ti. I ask the Order for a purifying probation for those offenses.’ Dutiyampi yācitabbo. And he should ask a second Tatiyampi yācitabbo. and a third time. Byattena bhikkhunā paṭibalena saṃgho ñāpetabbo— A competent and capable monk should then inform the Order:

‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṃgho. ‘Please, Venerables, I ask the Order to listen. Ayaṃ itthannāmo bhikkhu sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajji. This monk so-and-so has committed many offenses entailing suspension. Āpattipariyantaṃ na jānāti, rattipariyantaṃ na jānāti; He does not know the number of offenses or the number of days/ āpattipariyantaṃ nassarati, rattipariyantaṃ nassarati; he does not remember the number of offenses or the number of days/ āpattipariyante vematiko, rattipariyante vematiko. he has doubts about the number of offenses and the number of days. So saṃghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ suddhantaparivāsaṃ yācati. He is asking the Order for a purifying probation for those offenses. Yadi saṃghassa pattakallaṃ, saṃgho itthannāmassa bhikkhuno tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ suddhantaparivāsaṃ dadeyya. If it seems appropriate to the Order, the Order should give him a purifying probation for those offenses. Esā ñatti. This is the motion.

Suṇātu me, bhante, saṃgho. Please, Venerables, I ask the Order to listen. Ayaṃ itthannāmo bhikkhu sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajji. This monk so-and-so has committed many offenses entailing suspension. Āpattipariyantaṃ na jānāti, rattipariyantaṃ na jānāti; He does not know the number of offenses or the number of days/ āpattipariyantaṃ nassarati, rattipariyantaṃ nassarati; he does not remember the number of offenses or the number of days/ āpattipariyante vematiko, rattipariyante vematiko. he has doubts about the number of offenses and the number of days. So saṃghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ suddhantaparivāsaṃ yācati. He is asking the Order for purifying probation for those offenses. Saṃgho itthannāmassa bhikkhuno tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ suddhantaparivāsaṃ deti. The Order gives him a purifying probation for those offenses. Yassāyasmato khamati itthannāmassa bhikkhuno tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ suddhantaparivāsassa dānaṃ, so tuṇhassa; Any monk who approves of giving him a purifying probation for those offenses should remain silent. yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya. Any monk who does not approve should speak up.

Dutiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi … pe … For the second time I speak on this matter. … tatiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi … pe …. For the third time I speak on this matter. …

Dinno saṃghena itthannāmassa bhikkhuno tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ suddhantaparivāso. The Order has given monk so-and-so a purifying probation for those offenses. Khamati saṃghassa, tasmā tuṇhī, evametaṃ dhārayāmī’ti. The Order approves and is therefore silent. I will remember it thus.’

Evaṃ kho, bhikkhave, suddhantaparivāso dātabbo; evaṃ parivāso dātabbo.

Kathañca, bhikkhave, suddhantaparivāso dātabbo? “When should purifying probation be given? Āpattipariyantaṃ na jānāti, rattipariyantaṃ na jānāti; Purifying probation should be given when: one does not know the number of offenses or the number of days; āpattipariyantaṃ nassarati, rattipariyantaṃ nassarati; one does not remember the number of offenses or the number of days; āpattipariyante vematiko, rattipariyante vematiko— one has doubts about the number of offenses and the number of days. suddhantaparivāso dātabbo.

Āpattipariyantaṃ jānāti, rattipariyantaṃ na jānāti; Purifying probation should be given when: one knows the number of offenses, but not the number of days; āpattipariyantaṃ sarati, rattipariyantaṃ nassarati; one remembers the number of offenses, but not the number of days; āpattipariyante nibbematiko, rattipariyante vematiko— one is certain about the number of offenses, but not the number of days. suddhantaparivāso dātabbo.

Āpattipariyantaṃ ekaccaṃ jānāti, ekaccaṃ na jānāti, rattipariyantaṃ na jānāti; Purifying probation should be given when: one knows some of the offenses but not others, and not the number of days; āpattipariyantaṃ ekaccaṃ sarati, ekaccaṃ nassarati, rattipariyantaṃ nassarati; one remembers some of offenses but not others, and not the number of days; āpattipariyante ekacce vematiko, ekacce nibbematiko, rattipariyante vematiko— one is certain about some of the offenses but not others, and not the number of days. suddhantaparivāso dātabbo.

Āpattipariyantaṃ na jānāti, rattipariyantaṃ ekaccaṃ jānāti, ekaccaṃ na jānāti; “Purifying probation should be given when: one does not know the number of offenses, but one knows some of the days but not others; āpattipariyantaṃ nassarati, rattipariyantaṃ ekaccaṃ sarati, ekaccaṃ nassarati; one does not remember the number of offenses, but one remembers some of the days but not others; āpattipariyante vematiko, rattipariyante ekacce vematiko, ekacce nibbematiko— one has doubts about the number of offenses, but one is certain about some of the days but not others. suddhantaparivāso dātabbo.

Āpattipariyantaṃ jānāti, rattipariyantaṃ ekaccaṃ jānāti, ekaccaṃ na jānāti; Purifying probation should be given when: one knows the number of offenses, and one knows some of the days but not others; āpattipariyantaṃ sarati, rattipariyantaṃ ekaccaṃ sarati, ekaccaṃ nassarati; one remembers the number of offenses, and one remembers some of the days but not others; āpattipariyante nibbematiko, rattipariyante ekacce vematiko, ekacce nibbematiko— one is certain about the number of offenses, and one is certain about some of the days but not others. suddhantaparivāso dātabbo.

Āpattipariyantaṃ ekaccaṃ jānāti, ekaccaṃ na jānāti; Purifying probation should be given when: one knows some of the offenses but not others, rattipariyantaṃ ekaccaṃ jānāti, ekaccaṃ na jānāti; and one knows some of the days but not others; āpattipariyantaṃ ekaccaṃ sarati, ekaccaṃ nassarati; one remembers some of offenses but not others, rattipariyantaṃ ekaccaṃ sarati, ekaccaṃ nassarati; and one remembers some of the days but not others; āpattipariyante ekacce vematiko, ekacce nibbematiko; one is certain about some of the offenses but not others, rattipariyante ekacce vematiko, ekacce nibbematiko— and one is certain about some of the days but not others. suddhantaparivāso dātabbo. Evaṃ kho, bhikkhave, suddhantaparivāso dātabbo.

Kathañca, bhikkhave, parivāso dātabbo? “When should probation be given? Āpattipariyantaṃ jānāti, rattipariyantaṃ jānāti; Probation should be given when: one knows the number of offenses and the number of days; āpattipariyantaṃ sarati, rattipariyantaṃ sarati; one remembers the number of offenses and the number of days; āpattipariyante nibbematiko, rattipariyante nibbematiko— one is certain about the number of offenses and the number of days. parivāso dātabbo.

Āpattipariyantaṃ na jānāti, rattipariyantaṃ jānāti; Probation should be given when: one does not know the number of offenses, but one knows the number of days; āpattipariyantaṃ nassarati, rattipariyantaṃ sarati, one is uncertain about the number of offenses, but certain about the number of days. āpattipariyante vematiko, rattipariyante nibbematiko— one is uncertain about the number of offenses, but certain about the number of days. parivāso dātabbo.

Āpattipariyantaṃ ekaccaṃ jānāti, ekaccaṃ na jānāti, rattipariyantaṃ jānāti; Probation should be given when: one knows some of the offenses but not others, and one knows the number of days; āpattipariyantaṃ ekaccaṃ sarati, ekaccaṃ nassarati, rattipariyantaṃ sarati; one remembers some of offenses but not others, and one remembers the number of days; āpattipariyante ekacce vematiko, ekacce nibbematiko, rattipariyante nibbematiko— one is certain about some of the offenses but not others, and certain about the number of days.” parivāso dātabbo. Evaṃ kho, bhikkhave, parivāso dātabbo”.

Parivāso niṭṭhito. The section of probation is finished.

3. Cattālīsaka The group of forty

Tena kho pana samayena aññataro bhikkhu parivasanto vibbhami. At one time a monk on probation disrobed. So puna paccāgantvā bhikkhū upasampadaṃ yāci. He then came back and asked the monks for full ordination. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. They told the Master and he said:

“Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto vibbhamati. “It may be that a monk on probation disrobes. Vibbhantakassa, bhikkhave, parivāso na ruhati. For one who has disrobed, the probation is suspended. So ce puna upasampajjati, tassa tadeva purimaṃ parivāsadānaṃ. If he is given the full ordination again, he continues the previous probationary process right away. Yo parivāso dinno sudinno, yo parivuttho suparivuttho, avaseso parivasitabbo. (1) The probation that was given is valid. The probation he has already undertaken is valid. The remainder is to be undertaken.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto sāmaṇero hoti. It may be that a monk on probation becomes a novice monk. Sāmaṇerassa, bhikkhave, parivāso na ruhati. For a novice monk, the probation is suspended. So ce puna upasampajjati, tassa tadeva purimaṃ parivāsadānaṃ. If he is given the full ordination again, he continues the previous probationary process right away. Yo parivāso dinno sudinno, yo parivuttho suparivuttho, avaseso parivasitabbo. (2) The probation that was given is valid. The probation he has already undertaken is valid. The remainder is to be undertaken.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto ummattako hoti. It may be that a monk on probation goes insane. Ummattakassa, bhikkhave, parivāso na ruhati. For one who is insane, the probation is suspended. So ce puna anummattako hoti, tassa tadeva purimaṃ parivāsadānaṃ. If he regains his sanity, he continues the previous probationary process right away. Yo parivāso dinno sudinno, yo parivuttho suparivuttho, avaseso parivasitabbo. (3) The probation that was given is valid. The probation he has already undertaken is valid. The remainder is to be undertaken.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto khittacitto hoti. It may be that a monk on probation becomes deranged. Khittacittassa, bhikkhave, parivāso na ruhati. For one who is deranged, the probation is suspended. So ce puna akhittacitto hoti, tassa tadeva purimaṃ parivāsadānaṃ. If he regains his mental balance, he continues the previous probationary process right away. Yo parivāso dinno sudinno, yo parivuttho suparivuttho, avaseso parivasitabbo. (4) The probation that was given is valid. The probation he has already undertaken is valid. The remainder is to be undertaken.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto vedanāṭṭo hoti. It may be that a monk on probation is overwhelmed by pain. Vedanāṭṭassa, bhikkhave, parivāso na ruhati. For one who is overwhelmed by pain, the probation is suspended. So ce puna avedanāṭṭo hoti, tassa tadeva purimaṃ parivāsadānaṃ. If he recovers, he continues the previous probationary process right away. Yo parivāso dinno sudinno, yo parivuttho suparivuttho, avaseso parivasitabbo. (5) The probation that was given is valid. The probation he has already undertaken is valid. The remainder is to be undertaken.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhipiyyati. It may be that a monk on probation is ejected for not seeing an offense. Ukkhittakassa, bhikkhave, parivāso na ruhati. For one who is ejected, the probation is suspended. So ce puna osāriyyati, tassa tadeva purimaṃ parivāsadānaṃ. If he is re-admitted, he continues the previous probationary process right away. Yo parivāso dinno sudinno, yo parivuttho suparivuttho, avaseso parivasitabbo. (6) The probation that was given is valid. The probation he has already undertaken is valid. The remainder is to be undertaken.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhipiyyati. It may be that a monk on probation is ejected for not making amends for an offense. Ukkhittakassa, bhikkhave, parivāso na ruhati. For one who is ejected, the probation is suspended. So ce puna osāriyyati, tassa tadeva purimaṃ parivāsadānaṃ. If he is re-admitted, he continues the previous probationary process right away. Yo parivāso dinno sudinno, yo parivuttho suparivuttho, avaseso parivasitabbo. (7) The probation that was given is valid. The probation he has already undertaken is valid. The remainder is to be undertaken.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā, appaṭinissagge, ukkhipiyyati. It may be that a monk on probation is ejected for not giving up a bad view. Ukkhittakassa, bhikkhave, parivāso na ruhati. For one who is ejected, the probation is suspended. So ce puna osāriyyati, tassa tadeva purimaṃ parivāsadānaṃ. If he is re-admitted, he continues the previous probationary process right away. Yo parivāso dinno sudinno, yo parivuttho suparivuttho, avaseso parivasitabbo. (8) The probation that was given is valid. The probation he has already undertaken is valid. The remainder is to be undertaken.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu mūlāyapaṭikassanāraho vibbhamati. “It may be that a monk deserving to be sent back to the beginning disrobes. Vibbhantakassa, bhikkhave, mūlāyapaṭikassanā na ruhati. For one who has disrobed, the sending back to the beginning is suspended. So ce puna upasampajjati, tassa tadeva purimaṃ parivāsadānaṃ. If he is given the full ordination again, he continues the previous probationary process right away. Yo parivāso dinno sudinno, yo parivuttho suparivuttho. The probation that was given is valid. The probation he has already undertaken is valid. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo. (9) That monk is to be sent back to the beginning.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu mūlāyapaṭikassanāraho sāmaṇero hoti … pe … It may be that a monk deserving to be sent back to the beginning becomes a novice monk … ummattako hoti … pe … goes insane … khittacitto hoti … pe … becomes deranged … vedanāṭṭo hoti … pe … is overwhelmed by pain … āpattiyā adassane ukkhipiyyati … pe … is ejected for not seeing an offense … āpattiyā appaṭikamme ukkhipiyyati … pe … is ejected for not making amends for an offense … pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā, appaṭinissagge, ukkhipiyyati. is ejected for not giving up a bad view. Ukkhittakassa, bhikkhave, mūlāyapaṭikassanā na ruhati. For one who is ejected, the sending back to the beginning is suspended. So ce puna osāriyyati, tassa tadeva purimaṃ parivāsadānaṃ. If he is re-admitted, he continues the previous probationary process right away. Yo parivāso dinno sudinno, yo parivuttho suparivuttho. The probation that was given is valid. The probation he has already undertaken is valid. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo. (16) That monk is to be sent back to the beginning.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu mānattāraho vibbhamati. “It may be that a monk deserving the trial period of six days disrobes. Vibbhantakassa, bhikkhave, mānattadānaṃ na ruhati. For one who has disrobed, the giving of the trial period is suspended. So ce puna upasampajjati, tassa tadeva purimaṃ parivāsadānaṃ. If he is given the full ordination again, he continues the previous probationary process right away. Yo parivāso dinno sudinno, yo parivuttho suparivuttho. The probation that was given is valid. The probation he has undertaken is valid. Tassa bhikkhuno mānattaṃ dātabbaṃ. (17) That monk is to be given the trial period.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu mānattāraho sāmaṇero hoti … pe … It may be that a monk deserving the trial period of six days becomes a novice monk … ummattako hoti … pe … goes insane … khittacitto hoti … pe … becomes deranged … vedanāṭṭo hoti … pe … is overwhelmed by pain … āpattiyā adassane, ukkhipiyyati … pe … is ejected for not seeing an offense … āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhipiyyati … pe … is ejected for not making amends for an offense … pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā, appaṭinissagge, ukkhipiyyati. is ejected for not giving up a bad view. Ukkhittakassa, bhikkhave, mānattadānaṃ na ruhati. For one who is ejected, the giving of the trial period is suspended. So ce puna osāriyyati, tassa tadeva purimaṃ parivāsadānaṃ. If he is re-admitted, he continues the previous probationary process right away. Yo parivāso dinno sudinno, yo parivuttho suparivuttho. The probation that was given is valid. The probation he has undertaken is valid. Tassa bhikkhuno mānattaṃ dātabbaṃ. (24) That monk is to be given the trial period.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu mānattaṃ caranto vibbhamati. “It may be that a monk undertaking the trial period of six days disrobes. Vibbhantakassa, bhikkhave, mānattacariyā na ruhati. For one who has disrobed, the trial period is suspended. So ce puna upasampajjati tassa tadeva purimaṃ parivāsadānaṃ. If he is given the full ordination again, he continues the previous probationary process right away. Yo parivāso dinno sudinno, yo parivuttho suparivuttho; The probation that was given is valid. The probation he has undertaken is valid. yaṃ mānattaṃ dinnaṃ sudinnaṃ, yaṃ mānattaṃ ciṇṇaṃ suciṇṇaṃ, avasesaṃ caritabbaṃ. (25) The trial period that was given is valid. The trial period he has already undertaken is valid. The remainder is to be undertaken.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu mānattaṃ caranto sāmaṇero hoti … pe … It may be that a monk undertaking the trial period of six days becomes a novice monk … ummattako hoti … pe … goes insane … khittacitto hoti … pe … becomes deranged … vedanāṭṭo hoti … pe … is overwhelmed by pain … āpattiyā adassane, ukkhipiyyati … pe … is ejected for not seeing an offense … āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhipiyyati … pe … is ejected for not making amends for an offense … pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā, appaṭinissagge, ukkhipiyyati. is ejected for not giving up a bad view. Ukkhittakassa, bhikkhave, mānattacariyā na ruhati. For one who is ejected, the trial period is suspended. So ce puna osāriyyati, tassa tadeva purimaṃ parivāsadānaṃ. If he is re-admitted, he continues the previous probationary process right away. Yo parivāso dinno sudinno, yo purivuttho suparivuttho; The probation that was given is valid. The probation he has undertaken is valid. yaṃ mānattaṃ dinnaṃ sudinnaṃ, yaṃ mānattaṃ ciṇṇaṃ suciṇṇaṃ, avasesaṃ caritabbaṃ. (32) The trial period that was given is valid. The trial period he has undertaken is valid. The remainder is to be undertaken.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu abbhānāraho vibbhamati. “It may be that a monk deserving rehabilitation disrobes. Vibbhantakassa, bhikkhave, abbhānaṃ na ruhati. For one who has disrobed, the rehabilitation is suspended. So ce puna upasampajjati, tassa tadeva purimaṃ parivāsadānaṃ. If he is given the full ordination again, he continues the previous probationary process right away. Yo parivāso dinno sudinno, yo parivuttho suparivuttho; The probation that was given is valid. The probation he has undertaken is valid. yaṃ mānattaṃ dinnaṃ sudinnaṃ, yaṃ mānattaṃ ciṇṇaṃ suciṇṇaṃ. The trial period of six days that was given is valid. The trial period he has undertaken is valid. So bhikkhu abbhetabbo. (33) That monk is to be rehabilitated.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu abbhānāraho sāmaṇero hoti … pe … It may be that a monk deserving rehabilitation becomes a novice monk … ummattako hoti … pe … goes insane … khittacitto hoti … pe … becomes deranged … vedanāṭṭo hoti … pe … is overwhelmed by pain … āpattiyā adassane, ukkhipiyyati … pe … is ejected for not seeing an offense … āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhipiyyati … pe … is ejected for not making amends for an offense … pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā, appaṭinissagge, ukkhipiyyati. is ejected for not giving up a bad view. Ukkhittakassa, bhikkhave, abbhānaṃ na ruhati. For one who is ejected, the rehabilitation is suspended. So ce puna osāriyyati, tassa tadeva purimaṃ parivāsadānaṃ. If he is re-admitted, he continues the previous probationary process right away. Yo parivāso dinno sudinno, yo parivuttho suparivuttho; The probation that was given is valid. The probation he has undertaken is valid. yaṃ mānattaṃ dinnaṃ sudinnaṃ, yaṃ mānattaṃ ciṇṇaṃ suciṇṇaṃ. The trial period of six days that was given is valid. The trial period he has undertaken is valid. So bhikkhu abbhetabbo. (40) That monk is to be rehabilitated.”

Cattālīsakaṃ samattaṃ. The group of forty is finished.

4. Chattiṃsaka The group of thirty-six

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇā appaṭicchannāyo. “It may be that a monk on probation commits a number of offenses entailing suspension—specified and unconcealed. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo. (1) That monk is to be sent back to the beginning.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇā paṭicchannāyo. It may be that a monk on probation commits a number of offenses entailing suspension—specified and concealed. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo. That monk is to be sent back to the beginning. Yathāpaṭicchannānañcassa āpattīnaṃ purimāya āpattiyā samodhānaparivāso dātabbo. (2) He should then be given probation according to the length of the concealment of the offenses and simultaneously with the probation for the previous offense.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇā paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi. It may be that a monk on probation commits a number of offenses entailing suspension—specified and both concealed and unconcealed. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo. That monk is to be sent back to the beginning. Yathāpaṭicchannānañcassa āpattīnaṃ purimāya āpattiyā samodhānaparivāso dātabbo. (3) He should then be given probation according to the length of the concealment of the offenses and simultaneously with the probation for the previous offense.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati aparimāṇā appaṭicchannāyo … pe … It may be that a monk on probation commits a number of offenses entailing suspension—unspecified and unconcealed … aparimāṇā paṭicchannāyo … pe … unspecified and concealed … aparimāṇā paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi … pe … unspecified and both concealed and unconcealed … parimāṇāyopi aparimāṇāyopi appaṭicchannāyo … pe … unconcealed and both specified and unspecified … parimāṇāyopi aparimāṇāyopi paṭicchannāyo … pe … concealed and both specified and unspecified … parimāṇāyopi aparimāṇāyopi paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi. both concealed and unconcealed and both specified and unspecified. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo. That monk is to be sent back to the beginning. Yathāpaṭicchannānañcassa āpattīnaṃ purimāya āpattiyā samodhānaparivāso dātabbo. (9) He should then be given probation according to the length of the concealment of the offenses and simultaneously with the probation for the previous offense.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu mānattāraho … pe … It may be that a monk who deserves the trial period of six days … mānattaṃ caranto … pe … who is undertaking the trial period of six days … (yathāparivāsaṃ tathā vitthāretabbaṃ) To be expanded as for probation. abbhānāraho antarā sambahulā saṃghādisesā, āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇā appaṭicchannāyo … pe … who deserves rehabilitation commits a number of offenses entailing suspension—specified and unconcealed … parimāṇā paṭicchannāyo … pe … specified and concealed … parimāṇā paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi … pe … specified and both concealed and unconcealed … aparimāṇā appaṭicchannāyo … pe … unspecified and unconcealed … aparimāṇā paṭicchannāyo … pe … unspecified and concealed … aparimāṇā paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi … pe … unspecified and both concealed and unconcealed … parimāṇāyopi aparimāṇāyopi appaṭicchannāyo … pe … unconcealed and both specified and unspecified … parimāṇāyopi aparimāṇāyopi paṭicchannāyo … pe … concealed and both specified and unspecified … parimāṇāyopi aparimāṇāyopi paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi. both concealed and unconcealed and both specified and unspecified. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo. That monk is to be sent back to the beginning. Yathāpaṭicchannānañcassa āpattīnaṃ purimāya āpattiyā samodhānaparivāso dātabbo. (36) He should then be given probation according to the length of the concealment of the offenses and simultaneously with the probation for the previous offense.”

Chattiṃsakaṃ samattaṃ. The group of thirty-six is finished.

5. Mānattasata The group of one hundred on the trial period of six days

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjitvā appaṭicchādetvā vibbhamati. “It may be that a monk commits many unconcealed offenses entailing suspension and then disrobes. So puna upasampanno tā āpattiyo nacchādeti. Being re-ordained, he does not conceal those offenses. Tassa, bhikkhave, bhikkhuno mānattaṃ dātabbaṃ. (1) That monk should be given the trial period of six days.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjitvā appaṭicchādetvā vibbhamati. It may be that a monk commits many unconcealed offenses entailing suspension and then disrobes. So puna upasampanno tā āpattiyo chādeti. Being re-ordained, he conceals those offenses. Tassa, bhikkhave, bhikkhuno pacchimasmiṃ āpattikkhandhe yathāpaṭicchanne parivāsaṃ datvā mānattaṃ dātabbaṃ. (2) That monk should be given probation according to the length of the subsequent concealment of that group of offenses, and he should then be given the trial period of six days.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjitvā paṭicchādetvā vibbhamati. It may be that a monk commits many concealed offenses entailing suspension and then disrobes. So puna upasampanno tā āpattiyo nacchādeti. Being re-ordained, he does not conceal those offenses. Tassa, bhikkhave, bhikkhuno purimasmiṃ āpattikkhandhe yathāpaṭicchanne parivāsaṃ datvā mānattaṃ dātabbaṃ. (3) That monk should be given probation according to the length of the earlier concealment of that group of offenses, and he should then be given the trial period of six days.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjitvā paṭicchādetvā vibbhamati. It may be that a monk commits many concealed offenses entailing suspension and then disrobes. So puna upasampanno tā āpattiyo chādeti. Being re-ordained, he conceals those offenses. Tassa, bhikkhave, bhikkhuno purimasmiñca pacchimasmiñca āpattikkhandhe yathāpaṭicchanne parivāsaṃ datvā mānattaṃ dātabbaṃ. (4) That monk should be given probation according to the length of the earlier and subsequent concealment of that group of offenses, and he should then be given the trial period of six days.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati. “It may be that a monk commits many offenses entailing suspension, Tassa honti āpattiyo paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi. both concealed and unconcealed, So vibbhamitvā puna upasampanno yā āpattiyo pubbe chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nacchādeti; and then disrobes. Being re-ordained, he does not conceal any of those offenses. yā āpattiyo pubbe nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nacchādeti. Tassa, bhikkhave, bhikkhuno purimasmiṃ āpattikkhandhe yathāpaṭicchanne parivāsaṃ datvā mānattaṃ dātabbaṃ. (5) That monk should be given probation according to the length of the earlier concealment of that group of offenses, and he should then be given the trial period of six days.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati. It may be that a monk commits many offenses entailing suspension, Tassa honti āpattiyo paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi. both concealed and unconcealed, So vibbhamitvā puna upasampanno yā āpattiyo pubbe chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nacchādeti; and then disrobes. Being re-ordained, he does not conceal those offenses he previously concealed, yā āpattiyo pubbe nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā chādeti. but he conceals those offenses he previously did not conceal. Tassa, bhikkhave, bhikkhuno purimasmiñca pacchimasmiñca āpattikkhandhe yathāpaṭicchanne parivāsaṃ datvā mānattaṃ dātabbaṃ. (6) That monk should be given probation according to the length of the earlier and subsequent concealment of that group of offenses, and he should then be given the trial period of six days.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati. It may be that a monk commits many offenses entailing suspension, Tassa honti āpattiyo paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi. both concealed and unconcealed, So vibbhamitvā puna upasampanno yā āpattiyo pubbe chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā chādeti; and then disrobes. Being re-ordained, he conceals those offenses he previously concealed, yā āpattiyo pubbe nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nacchādeti. but he does not conceal those offenses he previously did not conceal. Tassa, bhikkhave, bhikkhuno purimasmiñca pacchimasmiñca āpattikkhandhe yathāpaṭicchanne parivāsaṃ datvā mānattaṃ dātabbaṃ. (7) That monk should be given probation according to the length of the earlier and subsequent concealment of that group of offenses, and he should then be given the trial period of six days.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati. It may be that a monk commits many offenses entailing suspension, Tassa honti āpattiyo paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi. both concealed and unconcealed, So vibbhamitvā puna upasampanno yā āpattiyo pubbe chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā chādeti; and then disrobes. Being re-ordained, he conceals all those offenses. yā āpattiyo pubbe nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā chādeti. Tassa, bhikkhave, bhikkhuno purimasmiñca pacchimasmiñca āpattikkhandhe yathāpaṭicchanne parivāsaṃ datvā mānattaṃ dātabbaṃ. (8) That monk should be given probation according to the length of the earlier and subsequent concealment of that group of offenses, and he should then be given the trial period of six days.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati. “It may be that a monk commits many offenses entailing suspension. Ekaccā āpattiyo jānāti, ekaccā āpattiyo na jānāti. He knows about some of the offenses, but not others. Yā āpattiyo jānāti tā āpattiyo chādeti. He conceals the offenses he knows about, Yā āpattiyo na jānāti tā āpattiyo nacchādeti. but not those he does not know about. So vibbhamitvā puna upasampanno yā āpattiyo pubbe jānitvā chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā jānitvā nacchādeti; He then disrobes. Being re-ordained and having found out about all the offenses, he conceals none of them. yā āpattiyo pubbe ajānitvā nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā jānitvā nacchādeti. Tassa, bhikkhave, bhikkhuno purimasmiṃ āpattikkhandhe yathāpaṭicchanne parivāsaṃ datvā mānattaṃ dātabbaṃ. (9) That monk should be given probation according to the length of the earlier concealment of that group of offenses, and he should then be given the trial period of six days.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati. It may be that a monk commits many offenses entailing suspension. Ekaccā āpattiyo jānāti, ekaccā āpattiyo na jānāti. Being re-ordained and having found out about all the offenses, he does not conceal those offenses he previously knew about, yā āpattiyo pubbe ajānitvā nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā jānitvā chādeti. but he conceals those he did not know about. Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati. “It may be that a monk commits many offenses entailing suspension. Ekaccāsu āpattīsu nibbematiko, ekaccāsu āpattīsu vematiko. (20) That monk should be given probation according to the length of the earlier and subsequent concealment of that group of offenses, and he should then be given the trial period of six days.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjitvā appaṭicchādetvā sāmaṇero hoti … pe … “It may be that a monk commits many unconcealed offenses entailing suspension and then becomes a novice monk … ummattako hoti … pe … goes insane … khittacitto hoti … pe … becomes deranged … (yathā heṭṭhā tathā vitthāretabbaṃ) To be expanded as above. vedanāṭṭo hoti … pe … is overwhelmed by pain … tassa honti āpattiyo paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi … pe … both concealed and unconcealed … ekaccā āpattiyo jānāti, ekaccā āpattiyo na jānāti … pe … he knows about some of the offenses, but not others … ekaccā āpattiyo sarati, ekaccā āpattiyo nassarati … pe … he remembers some of the offenses, but not others … ekaccāsu āpattīsu nibbematiko, ekaccāsu āpattīsu vematiko. he is certain about some of the offenses, but uncertain about others. Yāsu āpattīsu nibbematiko tā āpattiyo chādeti; He conceals the offenses he is certain about, yāsu āpattīsu vematiko tā āpattiyo nacchādeti. but not those he is uncertain about. So vedanāṭṭo hoti. He then becomes overwhelmed with pain. So puna avedanāṭṭo hutvā yā āpattiyo pubbe nibbematiko chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko nacchādeti; When he recovers and having become certain about all the offenses, he conceals none of them. … yā āpattiyo pubbe vematiko nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko nacchādeti … pe … yā āpattiyo pubbe nibbematiko chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko nacchādeti; having become certain about all the offenses, he does not conceal those offenses he previously was certain about, yā āpattiyo pubbe vematiko nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko chādeti … pe … but he conceals those he was uncertain about. … yā āpattiyo pubbe nibbematiko chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko chādeti; having become certain about all the offenses, he conceals those offenses he previously was certain about, yā āpattiyo pubbe vematiko nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko nacchādeti … pe … but not those he was uncertain about. … yā āpattiyo pubbe nibbematiko chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko chādeti; having become certain about all the offenses, he conceals all of them. yā āpattiyo pubbe vematiko nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko chādeti. Tassa, bhikkhave, bhikkhuno purimasmiñca pacchimasmiñca āpattikkhandhe yathāpaṭicchanne parivāsaṃ datvā mānattaṃ dātabbaṃ. (100) That monk should be given probation according to the length of the earlier and subsequent concealment of that group of offenses, and he should then be given the trial period of six days.”

Mānattasataṃ niṭṭhitaṃ. The group of one hundred on the trial period of six days is finished.

6. Samūlāyasamodhānaparivāsacatussata The group of four hundred on simultaneous probation with sending back to the beginning

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjitvā appaṭicchādetvā vibbhamati. “It may be that a monk on probation commits many unconcealed offenses entailing suspension, and then disrobes. So puna upasampanno tā āpattiyo nacchādeti. Being re-ordained, he does not conceal those offenses. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo. (1) That monk is to be sent back to the beginning.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjitvā appaṭicchādetvā vibbhamati. It may be that a monk on probation commits many unconcealed offenses entailing suspension, and then disrobes. So puna upasampanno tā āpattiyo chādeti. Being re-ordained, he conceals those offenses. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo. That monk is to be sent back to the beginning. Yathāpaṭicchannānañcassa āpattīnaṃ purimāya āpattiyā samodhānaparivāso dātabbo. (2) He is then to be given probation according to the length of the concealment of those offenses and simultaneously with the probation for the previous offenses.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjitvā paṭicchādetvā vibbhamati. It may be that a monk on probation commits many concealed offenses entailing suspension, and then disrobes. So puna upasampanno tā āpattiyo nacchādeti. Being re-ordained, he does not conceal those offenses. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo. That monk is to be sent back to the beginning. Yathāpaṭicchannānañcassa āpattīnaṃ purimāya āpattiyā samodhānaparivāso dātabbo. (3) He is then to be given probation according to the length of the concealment of those offenses and simultaneously with the probation for the previous offenses.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjitvā paṭicchādetvā vibbhamati. (4) He is then to be given probation according to the length of the concealment of those offenses and simultaneously with the probation for the previous offenses.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati. “It may be that a monk on probation commits many offenses entailing suspension, Tassa honti āpattiyo paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi. both concealed and unconcealed, So vibbhamitvā puna upasampanno yā āpattiyo pubbe chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nacchādeti; and then disrobes. Being re-ordained, he conceals none of those offenses. yā āpattiyo pubbe nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nacchādeti. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo. That monk is to be sent back to the beginning. Yathāpaṭicchannānañcassa āpattīnaṃ purimāya āpattiyā samodhānaparivāso dātabbo. (5) He is then to be given probation according to the length of the concealment of those offenses and simultaneously with the probation for the previous offenses.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati. It may be that a monk on probation commits many offenses entailing suspension, Tassa honti āpattiyo paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi. both concealed and unconcealed, So vibbhamitvā puna upasampanno yā āpattiyo pubbe chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nacchādeti; and then disrobes. Being re-ordained, he does not conceal those offenses he previously concealed, yā āpattiyo pubbe nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā chādeti. but he conceals those he previously did not conceal. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo. That monk is to be sent back to the beginning. Yathāpaṭicchannānañcassa āpattīnaṃ purimāya āpattiyā samodhānaparivāso dātabbo. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo. That monk is to be sent back to the beginning. Yathāpaṭicchannānañcassa āpattīnaṃ purimāya āpattiyā samodhānaparivāso dātabbo. (20) He is then to be given probation according to the length of the concealment of those offenses and simultaneously with the probation for the previous offenses.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjitvā appaṭicchādetvā sāmaṇero hoti … pe … “It may be that a monk on probation commits many unconcealed offenses entailing suspension, and then becomes a novice monk … ummattako hoti … pe … goes insane … khittacitto hoti … pe … becomes deranged … vedanāṭṭo hoti … pe … is overwhelmed by pain … tassa honti āpattiyo paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi… pe … both concealed and unconcealed … (yathā heṭṭhā vitthāritaṃ tathā vitthāretabbaṃ) To be expanded as above. ekaccā āpattiyo jānāti, ekaccā āpattiyo na jānāti … pe … he knows about some of the offenses, but not others … ekaccā āpattiyo sarati, ekaccā āpattiyo nassarati … pe … he remembers some of the offenses, but not others … ekaccāsu āpattīsu nibbematiko, ekaccāsu āpattīsu vematiko. he is certain about some of the offenses, but uncertain about others. Yāsu āpattīsu nibbematiko tā āpattiyo chādeti; He conceals the offenses he is certain about, yāsu āpattīsu vematiko tā āpattiyo nacchādeti. but not those he is uncertain about. So vedanāṭṭo hoti. He then becomes overwhelmed with pain. So puna avedanāṭṭo hutvā yā āpattiyo pubbe nibbematiko chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko nacchādeti; When he recovers and having become certain about all the offenses, he conceals none of them. … yā āpattiyo pubbe vematiko nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko nacchādeti … pe … yā āpattiyo pubbe nibbematiko chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko nacchādeti; having become certain about all the offenses, he does not conceal those offenses he previously was certain about, yā āpattiyo pubbe vematiko nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko chādeti … pe … but he conceals those he was uncertain about. … yā āpattiyo pubbe nibbematiko chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko chādeti; having become certain about all the offenses, he conceals those offenses he previously was certain about, yā āpattiyo pubbe vematiko nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko nacchādeti … pe … but not those he was uncertain about. … yā āpattiyo pubbe nibbematiko chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko chādeti; having become certain about all the offenses, he conceals all of them. yā āpattiyo pubbe vematiko nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko chādeti. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo. That monk is to be sent back to the beginning. Yathāpaṭicchannānañcassa āpattīnaṃ purimāya āpattiyā samodhānaparivāso dātabbo. (100) He is then to be given probation according to the length of the concealment of those offenses and simultaneously with the probation for the previous offenses.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu mānattāraho … pe … “It may be that a monk who deserves the trial period of six days … mānattaṃ caranto … pe … who is undertaking the trial period of six days … abbhānāraho antarā sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjitvā appaṭicchādetvā vibbhamati … pe … who deserves rehabilitation commits many unconcealed offenses entailing suspension, and then disrobes. … (mānattāraho ca mānattacārī ca abbhānāraho ca yathā parivāso vitthārito tathā vitthāretabbo). (320) ‘Who deserves the trial period,’ ‘who is undertaking the trial period,’ and ‘who deserves rehabilitation’ are to be expanded as for ‘on probation’.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu abbhānāraho antarā sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjitvā appaṭicchādetvā sāmaṇero hoti … pe … It may be that a monk who deserves rehabilitation commits many unconcealed offenses entailing suspension, and then becomes a novice monk … ummattako hoti … pe … goes insane … khittacitto hoti … pe … becomes deranged … vedanāṭṭo hoti … pe … is overwhelmed by pain … tassa honti āpattiyo paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi … pe … both concealed and unconcealed … ekaccā āpattiyo jānāti, ekaccā āpattiyo na jānāti … pe … he knows about some of the offenses, but not others … ekaccā āpattiyo sarati, ekaccā āpattiyo nassarati … pe … he remembers some of the offenses, but not others … ekaccāsu āpattīsu nibbematiko, ekaccāsu āpattīsu vematiko. he is certain about some of the offenses, but uncertain about others. Yāsu āpattīsu nibbematiko tā āpattiyo chādeti; He conceals the offenses he is certain about, yāsu āpattīsu vematiko tā āpattiyo nacchādeti. but not those he is uncertain about. So vedanāṭṭo hoti. He then becomes overwhelmed with pain. So puna avedanāṭṭo hutvā yā āpattiyo pubbe nibbematiko chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko nacchādeti; When he recovers and having become certain about all the offenses, he conceals none of them. … yā āpattiyo pubbe vematiko nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko nacchādeti … pe … yā āpattiyo pubbe nibbematiko chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko nacchādeti; having become certain about all the offenses, he does not conceal those offenses he previously was certain about, yā āpattiyo pubbe vematiko nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko chādeti … pe … but he conceals those he was uncertain about. … yā āpattiyo pubbe nibbematiko chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko chādeti; having become certain about all the offenses, he conceals those offenses he previously was certain about, yā āpattiyo pubbe vematiko nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko nacchādeti … pe … but not those he was uncertain about. … yā āpattiyo pubbe nibbematiko chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko chādeti; having become certain about all the offenses, he conceals all of them. yā āpattiyo pubbe vematiko nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko chādeti. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo. That monk is to be sent back to the beginning. Yathāpaṭicchannānañcassa āpattīnaṃ purimāya āpattiyā samodhānaparivāso dātabbo. (400) He is then to be given probation according to the length of the concealment of those offenses and simultaneously with the probation for the previous offenses.”

Samūlāyasamodhānaparivāsacatussataṃ niṭṭhitaṃ. The group of four hundred on simultaneous probation with being sent back to the beginning is finished.

7. Parimāṇādivāraaṭṭhaka The group of eight sections on specified, etc.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjitvā parimāṇā appaṭicchādetvā … pe … “It may be that a monk commits a number of offenses entailing suspension, specified and unconcealed … aparimāṇā appaṭicchādetvā … pe … unspecified and unconcealed … ekanāmā appaṭicchādetvā … pe … of one name and unconcealed … nānānāmā appaṭicchādetvā … pe … of various names and unconcealed … sabhāgā appaṭicchādetvā … pe … of one kind and unconcealed … visabhāgā appaṭicchādetvā … pe … of different kinds and unconcealed … vavatthitā appaṭicchādetvā … pe … of the same sort and unconcealed … sambhinnā appaṭicchādetvā vibbhamati … pe … of various sorts and unconcealed, and then disrobes. …” (yathā heṭṭhā tathā vitthāretabbaṃ). To be expanded as above.

Parimāṇādivāraaṭṭhakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ. The group of eight sections on specified, etc. is finished.

8. Dvebhikkhuvāraekādasaka The group of eleven sections on two monks

Dve bhikkhū saṃghādisesaṃ āpannā honti. Two monks have each committed an offense entailing suspension, Te saṃghādisese saṃghādisesadiṭṭhino honti. and they regard it as an offense entailing suspension. Eko chādeti, eko nacchādeti. One conceals his offense, but not the other. Yo chādeti so dukkaṭaṃ desāpetabbo. The one who conceals it is to confess an act of wrong conduct. Yathāpaṭicchanne cassa parivāsaṃ datvā ubhinnampi mānattaṃ dātabbaṃ. (1) He should be given probation according to the length of the concealment of that offense, and both should then be given the trial period of six days.

Dve bhikkhū saṃghādisesaṃ āpannā honti. Two monks have each committed an offense entailing suspension, Te saṃghādisese vematikā honti. but they have doubts about whether they have. Eko chādeti, eko nacchādeti. One conceals his offense, but not the other. Yo chādeti so dukkaṭaṃ desāpetabbo. The one who conceals it is to confess an act of wrong conduct. Yathāpaṭicchanne cassa parivāsaṃ datvā ubhinnampi mānattaṃ dātabbaṃ. (2) He should be given probation according to the length of the concealment of that offense, and both should then be given the trial period of six days.

Dve bhikkhū saṃghādisesaṃ āpannā honti. Two monks have each committed an offense entailing suspension, Te saṃghādisese missakadiṭṭhino honti. but they regard it as mixed with other offenses. Eko chādeti, eko nacchādeti. One conceals his offense, but not the other. Yo chādeti so dukkaṭaṃ desāpetabbo. The one who conceals it is to confess an act of wrong conduct. Yathāpaṭicchanne cassa parivāsaṃ datvā ubhinnampi mānattaṃ dātabbaṃ. (3) He should be given probation according to the length of the concealment of that offense, and both should then be given the trial period of six days.

Dve bhikkhū missakaṃ āpannā honti. Two monks have each committed an offense entailing suspension mixed with other offenses, Te missake saṃghādisesadiṭṭhino honti. but they regard them as offenses entailing suspension. Eko chādeti, eko nacchādeti. One conceals his offenses, but not the other. Yo chādeti so dukkaṭaṃ desāpetabbo. The one who conceals them is to confess an act of wrong conduct. Yathāpaṭicchanne cassa parivāsaṃ datvā ubhinnampi mānattaṃ dātabbaṃ. (4) He should be given probation according to the length of the concealment, and both should then be given the trial period of six days.

Dve bhikkhū missakaṃ āpannā honti. Two monks have each committed an offense entailing suspension mixed with other offenses, Te missake missakadiṭṭhino honti. and they regard them as a mix of offenses. Eko chādeti, eko nacchādeti. One conceals his offenses, but not the other. Yo chādeti so dukkaṭaṃ desāpetabbo. The one who conceals them is to confess an act of wrong conduct. Yathāpaṭicchanne cassa parivāsaṃ datvā ubhinnampi mānattaṃ dātabbaṃ. (5) He should be given probation according to the length of the concealment, and both should then be given the trial period of six days.

Dve bhikkhū suddhakaṃ āpannā honti. Two monks have each committed a light offense, Te suddhake saṃghādisesadiṭṭhino honti. but they regard it as an offense entailing suspension. Eko chādeti, eko nacchādeti. One conceals his offense, but not the other. Yo chādeti so dukkaṭaṃ desāpetabbo. The one who conceals it is to confess an act of wrong conduct. Ubhopi yathādhammaṃ kārāpetabbā. (6) Both are then to be dealt with according to the rule.

Dve bhikkhū suddhakaṃ āpannā honti. Two monks have each committed a light offense, Te suddhake suddhakadiṭṭhino honti. and they regard it as a light offense. Eko chādeti, eko nacchādeti. One conceals his offense, but not the other. Yo chādeti so dukkaṭaṃ desāpetabbo. The one who conceals it is to confess an act of wrong conduct. Ubhopi yathādhammaṃ kārāpetabbā. (7) Both are then to be dealt with according to the rule.

Dve bhikkhū saṃghādisesaṃ āpannā honti. Two monks have each committed an offense entailing suspension, Te saṃghādisese saṃghādisesadiṭṭhino honti. and they regard it as an offense entailing suspension. Ekassa hoti ārocessāmīti, ekassa hoti na ārocessāmīti. One thinks, “I will inform;” the other thinks, “I will not inform.” So paṭhamampi yāmaṃ chādeti, dutiyampi yāmaṃ chādeti, tatiyampi yāmaṃ chādeti— He then conceals it for the first part of the night, for the second part of the night, and for the third part of the night. uṭṭhite aruṇe channā hoti āpatti. If he is still concealing it at dawn, he has committed an offense Yo chādeti so dukkaṭaṃ desāpetabbo. and is to confess an act of wrong conduct. Yathāpaṭicchanne cassa parivāsaṃ datvā ubhinnampi mānattaṃ dātabbaṃ. (8) He should be given probation according to the length of the concealment of that offense, and both should then be given the trial period of six days.

Dve bhikkhū saṃghādisesaṃ āpannā honti. Two monks have each committed an offense entailing suspension, Te saṃghādisese saṃghādisesadiṭṭhino honti. and they regard it as an offense entailing suspension. Te gacchanti ārocessāmāti. They go, thinking, “We will inform.” Ekassa antarāmagge makkhadhammo uppajjati na ārocessāmīti. On their way, one of them decides to conceal it, thinking, “I will not inform.” So paṭhamampi yāmaṃ chādeti, dutiyampi yāmaṃ chādeti, tatiyampi yāmaṃ chādeti— He then conceals it for the first part of the night, for the second part of the night, and for the third part of the night. uṭṭhite aruṇe channā hoti āpatti. If he is still concealing it at dawn, he has committed an offense Yo chādeti so dukkaṭaṃ desāpetabbo. and is to confess an act of wrong conduct. Yathāpaṭicchanne cassa parivāsaṃ datvā ubhinnampi mānattaṃ dātabbaṃ. (9) He should be given probation according to the length of the concealment of that offense, and both should then be given the trial period of six days.

Dve bhikkhū saṃghādisesaṃ āpannā honti. Two monks have each committed an offense entailing suspension. Te saṃghādisese saṃghādisesadiṭṭhino honti. They regard it as an offense entailing suspension, Te ummattakā honti. but then go insane. Te pacchā anummattakā hutvā eko chādeti, eko nacchādeti. When they regain their sanity, one conceals his offense, but not the other. Yo chādeti so dukkaṭaṃ desāpetabbo. The one who conceals it is to confess an act of wrong conduct. Yathāpaṭicchanne cassa parivāsaṃ datvā ubhinnampi mānattaṃ dātabbaṃ. (10) He should be given probation according to the length of the concealment of that offense, and both should then be given the trial period of six days.

Dve bhikkhū saṃghādisesaṃ āpannā honti. Two monks have each committed an offense entailing suspension. Te pātimokkhe uddissamāne evaṃ vadanti— During the recitation of the Monastic Code, they say, ‘idāneva kho mayaṃ jānāma— “Just now did we find out ayampi kira dhammo suttāgato suttapariyāpanno anvaddhamāsaṃ uddesaṃ āgacchatī’ti. that this rule too has come down in the Monastic Code, is included in the Monastic Code, and comes up for recitation every half-month.” Te saṃghādisese saṃghādisesadiṭṭhino honti. They regard it as an offense entailing suspension. Eko chādeti, eko nacchādeti. One conceals his offense, but not the other. Yo chādeti so dukkaṭaṃ desāpetabbo. The one who conceals it is to confess an act of wrong conduct. Yathāpaṭicchanne cassa parivāsaṃ datvā ubhinnampi mānattaṃ dātabbaṃ. (11) He should be given probation according to the length of the concealment of that offense, and both should then be given the trial period of six days.

Dvebhikkhuvāraekādasakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ. The group of eleven sections on two monks is finished.

9. Mūlāyaavisuddhinavaka The group of nine on unpurified with sending back to the beginning

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi, ekanāmampi nānānāmampi, sabhāgampi visabhāgampi, vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. “It may be that a monk has committed many offenses entailing suspension, both specified and unspecified, both of the same name and of various names, both of the same kind and of various kinds, both of the same sort and of various sorts. So saṃghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yācati. He asks the Order for simultaneous probation for those offenses, Tassa saṃgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti. and the Order gives him that probation. So parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇāyo appaṭicchannāyo. While on probation, he commits many offenses entailing suspension—specified and unconcealed. So saṃghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati. He asks the Order to send him back to the beginning for those offenses, Taṃ saṃgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassati dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti; and it does. The legal procedure is legitimate, irreversible, and fit to stand. And the Order gives him simultaneous probation legitimately. adhammena mānattaṃ deti, adhammena abbheti. It then gives him the trial period of six days illegitimately, and the rehabilitation illegitimately. So, bhikkhave, bhikkhu avisuddho tāhi āpattīhi. (1) That monk is not purified from those offenses.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi, ekanāmampi nānānāmampi, sabhāgampi visabhāgampi, vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. It may be that a monk has committed many offenses entailing suspension, both specified and unspecified, both of the same name and of various names, both of the same kind and of various kinds, both of the same sort and of various sorts. So saṃghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yācati. He asks the Order for simultaneous probation for those offenses, Tassa saṃgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti. and the Order gives him that probation. So parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇāyo paṭicchannāyo. While on probation, he commits many offenses entailing suspension—specified and concealed. So saṃghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati. He asks the Order to send him back to the beginning for those offenses, Taṃ saṃgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassati dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti; and it does. The legal procedure is legitimate, irreversible, and fit to stand. And the Order gives him simultaneous probation legitimately. adhammena mānattaṃ deti, adhammena abbheti. It then gives him the trial period of six days illegitimately, and the rehabilitation illegitimately. So, bhikkhave, bhikkhu avisuddho tāhi āpattīhi. (2) That monk is not purified from those offenses.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi, ekanāmampi nānānāmampi, sabhāgampi visabhāgampi, vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. It may be that a monk has committed many offenses entailing suspension, both specified and unspecified, both of the same name and of various names, both of the same kind and of various kinds, both of the same sort and of various sorts. So saṃghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yācati. He asks the Order for simultaneous probation for those offenses, Tassa saṃgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti. and the Order gives him that probation. So parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇāyo paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi. While on probation, he commits many offenses entailing suspension—specified and both concealed and unconcealed. So saṃghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati. He asks the Order to send him back to the beginning for those offenses, Taṃ saṃgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassati dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti, adhammena mānattaṃ deti, adhammena abbheti. and it does. The legal procedure is legitimate, irreversible, and fit to stand. And the Order gives him simultaneous probation legitimately. It then gives him the trial period of six days illegitimately, and the rehabilitation illegitimately. So, bhikkhave, bhikkhu avisuddho tāhi āpattīhi. (3) That monk is not purified from those offenses.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi, ekanāmampi nānānāmampi, sabhāgampi visabhāgampi, vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. “It may be that a monk has committed many offenses entailing suspension, both specified and unspecified, both of the same name and of various names, both of the same kind and of various kinds, both of the same sort and of various sorts. So saṃghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yācati. He asks the Order for simultaneous probation for those offenses, Tassa saṃgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti. and the Order gives him that probation. So parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati aparimāṇāyo appaṭicchannāyo … pe … While on probation, he commits many offenses entailing suspension—unspecified and unconcealed … aparimāṇāyo paṭicchannāyo … pe … unspecified and concealed … aparimāṇāyo paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi … pe … unspecified and both concealed and unconcealed … parimāṇāyopi aparimāṇāyopi appaṭicchannāyo. unconcealed and both specified and unspecified. So saṃghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati. He asks the Order to send him back to the beginning for those offenses, Taṃ saṃgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassati dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti; and it does. The legal procedure is legitimate, irreversible, and fit to stand. And the Order gives him simultaneous probation legitimately. adhammena mānattaṃ deti, adhammena abbheti. It then gives him the trial period of six days illegitimately, and the rehabilitation illegitimately. So, bhikkhave, bhikkhu avisuddho tāhi āpattīhi. (4–7) That monk is not purified from those offenses.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi, ekanāmampi nānānāmampi, sabhāgampi visabhāgampi, vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. It may be that a monk has committed many offenses entailing suspension, both specified and unspecified, both of the same name and of various names, both of the same kind and of various kinds, both of the same sort and of various sorts. So saṃghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yācati. He asks the Order for simultaneous probation for those offenses, Tassa saṃgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti. and the Order gives him that probation. So parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇāyopi aparimāṇāyopi paṭicchannāyo. While on probation, he commits many offenses entailing suspension—concealed and both specified and unspecified. So saṃghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati. He asks the Order to send him back to the beginning for those offenses, Taṃ saṃgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassati dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti; and it does. The legal procedure is legitimate, irreversible, and fit to stand. And the Order gives him simultaneous probation legitimately. adhammena mānattaṃ deti, adhammena abbheti. It then gives him the trial period of six days illegitimately, and the rehabilitation illegitimately. So, bhikkhave, bhikkhu avisuddho tāhi āpattīhi. (8) That monk is not purified from those offenses.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi, ekanāmampi nānānāmampi, sabhāgampi visabhāgampi, vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. It may be that a monk has committed many offenses entailing suspension, both specified and unspecified, both of the same name and of various names, both of the same kind and of various kinds, both of the same sort and of various sorts. So saṃghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yācati. He asks the Order for simultaneous probation for those offenses, Tassa saṃgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti. and the Order gives him that probation. So parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇāyopi aparimāṇāyopi paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi. While on probation, he commits many offenses entailing suspension—both concealed and unconcealed and both specified and unspecified. So saṃghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati. He asks the Order to send him back to the beginning for those offenses, Taṃ saṃgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassati dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena; and it does. The legal procedure is legitimate, irreversible, and fit to stand. dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti; And the Order gives him simultaneous probation legitimately. adhammena mānattaṃ deti; It then gives him the trial period of six days illegitimately, adhammena abbheti. and the rehabilitation illegitimately. So, bhikkhave, bhikkhu avisuddho tāhi āpattīhi. (9) That monk is not purified from those offenses.”

Mūlāyaavisuddhinavakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ. The group of nine on unpurified with sending back to the beginning is finished.

10. Dutiyanavaka The second group of nine

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi … pe … “It may be that a monk has committed many offenses entailing suspension, both specified and unspecified, both of the same name and of various names, both of the same kind and of various kinds, vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. both of the same sort and of various sorts. So saṃghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yācati. He asks the Order for simultaneous probation for those offenses, Tassa saṃgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti, so parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇā appaṭicchannāyo. and the Order gives him that probation. While on probation, he commits many offenses entailing suspension—specified and unconcealed. So saṃghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati. He asks the Order to send him back to the beginning for those offenses, Taṃ saṃgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassati adhammikena kammena kuppena aṭṭhānārahena, adhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti; and it does. But the legal procedure is illegitimate, reversible, and unfit to stand. And the Order gives him simultaneous probation illegitimately. dhammena mānattaṃ deti, dhammena abbheti. It then gives him the trial period of six days legitimately, and the rehabilitation legitimately. So, bhikkhave, bhikkhu avisuddho tāhi āpattīhi. (1) That monk is not purified from those offenses.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi … pe … It may be that a monk has committed many offenses entailing suspension, both specified and unspecified, both of the same name and of various names, both of the same kind and of various kinds, vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. both of the same sort and of various sorts. While on probation, he commits many offenses entailing suspension—specified and both concealed and unconcealed. So saṃghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati. He asks the Order to send him back to the beginning for those offenses, Taṃ saṃgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassati adhammikena kammena kuppena aṭṭhānārahena, adhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti; and it does. 11. Tatiyanavaka The third group of nine

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi … pe … “It may be that a monk has committed many offenses entailing suspension, both specified and unspecified, both of the same name and of various names, both of the same kind and of various kinds, vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. both of the same sort and of various sorts. So saṃghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yācati. He asks the Order for simultaneous probation for those offenses, Tassa saṃgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti. and the Order gives him that probation. So parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇāyo appaṭicchannāyo. While on probation, he commits many offenses entailing suspension—specified and unconcealed. So saṃghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati. He asks the Order to send him back to the beginning for those offenses, Taṃ saṃgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassati adhammikena kammena kuppena aṭṭhānārahena, adhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti. and it does. But the legal procedure is illegitimate, reversible, and unfit to stand. And the Order gives him simultaneous probation illegitimately. So parivasāmīti maññamāno antarā sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇāyo appaṭicchannāyo. Thinking that he is on probation, he commits many offenses entailing suspension—specified and unconcealed. So tasmiṃ bhūmiyaṃ ṭhito purimāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattiyo sarati, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattiyo sarati. At this point, he remembers offenses committed while on probation for the former offenses, and he remembers offenses committed while on probation for the further offenses. Tassa evaṃ hoti— He considers all this ‘ahaṃ kho sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi … pe … vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. Sohaṃ saṃghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yāciṃ. Tassa me saṃgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ adāsi. Sohaṃ parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ parimāṇāyo appaṭicchannāyo. Sohaṃ saṃghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yāciṃ. Taṃ maṃ saṃgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassi adhammikena kammena kuppena aṭṭhānārahena, adhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ adāsi. Sohaṃ parivasāmīti maññamāno antarā sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ parimāṇāyo appaṭicchannāyo. Sohaṃ tasmiṃ bhūmiyaṃ ṭhito purimāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattiyo sarāmi, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattiyo sarāmi. Yannūnāhaṃ saṃghaṃ purimāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yāceyyaṃ dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ; and thinks, ‘Let me ask the Order to send me back to the beginning for all those offenses committed while on probation. And let the procedure be legitimate, irreversible, and fit to stand; let the simultaneous probation be legitimate; dhammena mānattaṃ, dhammena abbhānan’ti. let the trial period of six days be legitimate; and let the rehabilitation be legitimate.’ So saṃghaṃ purimāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ; He asks to be sent back to the beginning in this way, dhammena mānattaṃ, dhammena abbhānaṃ. Taṃ saṃgho purimāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, mūlāya paṭikassati dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti; and the Order sends him back to the beginning for those offenses committed while on probation. The procedure is legitimate, irreversible, and fit to stand. And the Order gives him simultaneous probation legitimately. dhammena mānattaṃ deti, dhammena abbheti. It also gives him the trial period of six days legitimately, and it rehabilitates him legitimately. So, bhikkhave, bhikkhu visuddho tāhi āpattīhi. (1) That monk is purified from those offenses.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi … pe … It may be that a monk has committed many offenses entailing suspension, both specified and unspecified, both of the same name and of various names, both of the same kind and of various kinds, vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. both of the same sort and of various sorts. Taṃ maṃ saṃgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassi, adhammikena kammena kuppena aṭṭhānārahena, adhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ adāsi. Sohaṃ parivasāmīti maññamāno antarā sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ parimāṇā paṭicchannāyo. Sohaṃ tasmiṃ bhūmiyaṃ ṭhito purimāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattiyo sarāmi, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattiyo sarāmi. Yannūnāhaṃ saṃghaṃ purimāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yāceyyaṃ dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ, dhammena mānattaṃ, dhammena abbhānan’ti. and thinks, ‘Let me ask the Order to send me back to the beginning for all those offenses committed while on probation. He asks to be sent back to the beginning in this way, Taṃ saṃgho purimāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, mūlāya paṭikassati dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti, dhammena mānattaṃ deti, dhammena abbheti. and the Order sends him back to the beginning for those offenses committed while on probation.
