At this point he remembers offenses committed while on probation for the former offenses, and he remembers offenses committed while on probation for the further offenses. Tassa evaṃ hoti— He considers all this ‘ahaṃ kho sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi … pe … vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. Sohaṃ saṃghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yāciṃ. Tassa me saṃgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ adāsi. Sohaṃ parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ parimāṇā paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi. Sohaṃ saṃghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yāciṃ. Taṃ maṃ saṃgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassi adhammikena kammena kuppena aṭṭhānārahena, adhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ adāsi. Sohaṃ parivasāmīti maññamāno antarā sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ parimāṇā paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi. Sohaṃ tasmiṃ bhūmiyaṃ ṭhito purimāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattiyo sarāmi, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattiyo sarāmi. Yannūnāhaṃ saṃghaṃ purimāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yāceyyaṃ dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ, dhammena mānattaṃ, dhammena abbhānan’ti. and thinks, ‘Let me ask the Order to send me back to the beginning for all those offenses committed while on probation. And let the procedure be legitimate, irreversible, and fit to stand; let the simultaneous probation be legitimate; let the trial period of six days be legitimate; and let the rehabilitation be legitimate.’ So saṃghaṃ purimāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ, dhammena mānattaṃ, dhammena abbhānaṃ. He asks to be sent back to the beginning in this way, Taṃ saṃgho purimāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, mūlāya paṭikassati dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti, dhammena mānattaṃ deti, dhammena abbheti. and the Order sends him back to the beginning for those offenses committed while on probation. The procedure is legitimate, irreversible, and fit to stand. And the Order gives him simultaneous probation legitimately. It also gives him the trial period of six days legitimately, and it rehabilitates him legitimately. So, bhikkhave, bhikkhu visuddho tāhi āpattīhi. (3) That monk is purified from those offenses.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi … pe … “It may be that a monk has committed many offenses entailing suspension, both specified and unspecified, both of the same name and of various names, both of the same kind and of various kinds, vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. both of the same sort and of various sorts. So saṃghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yācati. He asks the Order for simultaneous probation for those offenses, Tassa saṃgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti. and the Order gives him that probation. So parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati aparimāṇāyo appaṭicchannāyo … pe … While on probation, he commits many offenses entailing suspension—unspecified and unconcealed … aparimāṇāyo paṭicchannāyo … pe … unspecified and concealed … aparimāṇāyo paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi … pe … unspecified and both concealed and unconcealed … parimāṇāyopi aparimāṇāyopi appaṭicchannāyo. unconcealed and both specified and unspecified. So saṃghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati. He asks the Order to send him back to the beginning for those offenses, Taṃ saṃgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassi adhammikena kammena kuppena aṭṭhānārahena, adhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti. and it does. But the legal procedure is illegitimate, reversible, and unfit to stand. And the Order gives him simultaneous probation illegitimately. So parivasāmīti maññamāno … pe … Thinking that he is on probation … taṃ saṃgho purimāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, mūlāya paṭikassati dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti, dhammena mānattaṃ deti, dhammena abbheti. and the Order sends him back to the beginning for those offenses committed while on probation. The procedure is legitimate, irreversible, and fit to stand. And the Order gives him simultaneous probation legitimately. It also gives him the trial period of six days legitimately, and it rehabilitates him legitimately. So, bhikkhave, bhikkhu visuddho tāhi āpattīhi. (4–7) That monk is purified from those offenses.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi … pe … It may be that a monk has committed many offenses entailing suspension, both specified and unspecified, both of the same name and of various names, both of the same kind and of various kinds, vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. both of the same sort and of various sorts. So saṃghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yācati. He asks the Order for simultaneous probation for those offenses, Tassa saṃgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti. and the Order gives him that probation. So parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇāyopi aparimāṇāyopi paṭicchannāyo. While on probation, he commits many offenses entailing suspension—concealed and both specified and unspecified. So saṃghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati. He asks the Order to send him back to the beginning for those offenses, Taṃ saṃgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassati adhammikena kammena kuppena aṭṭhānārahena, adhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti. and it does. But the legal procedure is illegitimate, reversible, and unfit to stand. And the Order gives him simultaneous probation illegitimately. So parivasāmīti maññamāno antarā sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇāyopi aparimāṇāyopi paṭicchannāyo. Thinking that he is on probation, he commits many offenses entailing suspension—concealed and both specified and unspecified. So tasmiṃ bhūmiyaṃ ṭhito purimāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattiyo sarati, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattiyo sarati. At this point he remembers offenses committed while on probation for the former offenses, and he remembers offenses committed while on probation for the further offenses. Tassa evaṃ hoti— He considers all this ‘ahaṃ kho sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi … pe … vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. Sohaṃ saṃghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yāciṃ. Tassa me saṃgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ adāsi. Sohaṃ parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ parimāṇāyopi aparimāṇāyopi paṭicchannāyo. Sohaṃ saṃghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yāciṃ. Taṃ maṃ saṃgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassi adhammikena kammena kuppena aṭṭhānārahena, adhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ adāsi. Sohaṃ parivasāmīti maññamāno antarā sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ parimāṇāyopi aparimāṇāyopi paṭicchannāyo. Sohaṃ tasmiṃ bhūmiyaṃ ṭhito purimāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattiyo sarāmi, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattiyo sarāmi. Yannūnāhaṃ saṃghaṃ purimāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yāceyyaṃ dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ, dhammena mānattaṃ, dhammena abbhānan’ti. and thinks, ‘Let me ask the Order to send me back to the beginning for all those offenses committed while on probation. And let the procedure be legitimate, irreversible, and fit to stand; let the simultaneous probation be legitimate; let the trial period of six days be legitimate; and let the rehabilitation be legitimate.’ So saṃghaṃ purimāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ, dhammena mānattaṃ, dhammena abbhānaṃ. He asks to be sent back to the beginning in this way, Taṃ saṃgho purimāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, mūlāya paṭikassati dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti, dhammena mānattaṃ deti, dhammena abbheti. and the Order sends him back to the beginning for those offenses committed while on probation. The procedure is legitimate, irreversible, and fit to stand. And the Order gives him simultaneous probation legitimately. It also gives him the trial period of six days legitimately, and it rehabilitates him legitimately. So, bhikkhave, bhikkhu visuddho tāhi āpattīhi. (8) That monk is purified from those offenses.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi … pe … It may be that a monk has committed many offenses entailing suspension, both specified and unspecified, both of the same name and of various names, both of the same kind and of various kinds, vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. both of the same sort and of various sorts. He asks the Order to send him back to the beginning for those offenses, Taṃ saṃgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassati adhammikena kammena kuppena aṭṭhānārahena, adhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti. and it does. Thinking that he is on probation, he commits many offenses entailing suspension—both concealed and unconcealed and both specified and unspecified. So tasmiṃ bhūmiyaṃ ṭhito purimāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattiyo sarati, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattiyo sarati. Tassa evaṃ hoti— He considers all this ‘ahaṃ kho sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi … pe … vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. Sohaṃ saṃghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yāciṃ. Tassa me saṃgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ adāsi. Sohaṃ parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ parimāṇāyopi aparimāṇāyopi paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi. Sohaṃ saṃghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yāciṃ. Taṃ maṃ saṃgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassi adhammikena kammena kuppena aṭṭhānārahena, adhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ adāsi. Sohaṃ parivasāmīti maññamāno antarā sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ parimāṇāyopi aparimāṇāyopi paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi. Sohaṃ tasmiṃ bhūmiyaṃ ṭhito purimāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattiyo sarāmi, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattiyo sarāmi. Yannūnāhaṃ saṃghaṃ purimāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yāceyyaṃ dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ, dhammena mānattaṃ, dhammena abbhānan’ti. and thinks, ‘Let me ask the Order to send me back to the beginning for all those offenses committed while on probation. And let the procedure be legitimate, irreversible, and fit to stand; let the simultaneous probation be legitimate; let the trial period of six days be legitimate; and let the rehabilitation be legitimate.’ So saṃghaṃ purimāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, mūlāya paṭikassanaṃ yācati dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ, dhammena mānattaṃ, dhammena abbhānaṃ. He asks to be sent back to the beginning in this way, Taṃ saṃgho purimāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, mūlāya paṭikassati dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti, dhammena mānattaṃ deti, dhammena abbheti. and the Order sends him back to the beginning for those offenses committed while on probation. The procedure is legitimate, irreversible, and fit to stand. And the Order gives him simultaneous probation legitimately. It also gives him the trial period of six days legitimately, and it rehabilitates him legitimately. So, bhikkhave, bhikkhu visuddho tāhi āpattīhi”. (9) That monk is purified from those offenses.”

Tatiyanavakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ. The third group of nine is finished.

Samuccayakkhandhako tatiyo. The third chapter on various aspects of offenses entailing suspension is finished.

Tassuddānaṃ (The summary verses have not been translated.)

Appaṭicchannā ekāha,
dvīha tīha catūha ca;
Pañcāhapakkhadasannaṃ,
āpattimāha mahāmuni.

Suddhanto ca vibbhamanto,
parimāṇamukhaṃ dve bhikkhū;
Tattha saññino dve yathā,
vematikā tatheva ca.

Missakadiṭṭhino dve ca,
asuddhakekadiṭṭhino;
Dve ceva suddhadiṭṭhino.

Tatheva ca eko chādeti,
Atha makkhamatena ca;
Ummattakadesanañca,
Mūlā aṭṭhārasa visuddhato.

Ācariyānaṃ vibhajjapadānaṃ,
Tambapaṇṇidīpapasādakānaṃ;
Mahāvihāravāsīnaṃ,
Vācanā saddhammaṭṭhitiyāti.

Samuccayakkhandhako niṭṭhito. The chapter on various aspects of offenses entailing suspension is finished.
